    15	package stats // import "fortio.org/fortio/stats"
    16	
    17	import (
    18	        "bufio"
    19	        "bytes"
    20	        "errors"
    21	        "fmt"
    22	        "io"
    23	        "math"
    24	        "strconv"

    27	        "fortio.org/log"
    28	)
    29	
    30	// Counter is a type whose instances record values
    31	// and calculate stats (count, average, min, max, and stddev).
    32	type Counter struct {
    33	        Count        int64
    34	        Min          float64
    35	        Max          float64
    36	        Sum          float64
    37	        sumOfSquares float64
    38	}
    39	
    40	// Record records a data point.
    41	func (c *Counter) Record(v float64) {
    42	        c.RecordN(v, 1)
    43	}
    44	
    45	// RecordN efficiently records the same value N times.
    46	func (c *Counter) RecordN(v float64, n int) {
    47	        isFirst := (c.Count == 0)
    48	        c.Count += int64(n)
    49	        switch {
    50	        case isFirst:
    51	                c.Min = v
    52	                c.Max = v
    53	        case v < c.Min:
    54	                c.Min = v
    55	        case v > c.Max:
    56	                c.Max = v
    57	        }
    58	        s := v * float64(n)
    59	        c.Sum += s
    60	        c.sumOfSquares += (s * s)
    61	}
    62	
    63	// Avg returns the average.
    64	func (c *Counter) Avg() float64 {
    65	        if c.Count == 0 {
    66	                return 0.
    67	        }
    68	        return c.Sum / float64(c.Count)
    69	}
    70	
    71	// StdDev returns the standard deviation.
    72	func (c *Counter) StdDev() float64 {
    73	        if c.Count == 0 {
    74	                return 0.
    75	        }
    76	        fC := float64(c.Count)
    77	        sigma := (c.sumOfSquares - c.Sum*c.Sum/fC) / fC
    78	        // should never happen but it does
    79	        if sigma < 0 {
    80	                log.Warnf("Unexpected negative sigma for %+v: %g", c, sigma)
    81	                return 0
    82	        }
    83	        return math.Sqrt(sigma)
    84	}
    85	
    86	// Print prints stats.
    87	func (c *Counter) Print(out io.Writer, msg string) {
    88	        _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "%s : count %d avg %.8g +/- %.4g min %g max %g sum %.9g\n",
    89	                msg, c.Count, c.Avg(), c.StdDev(), c.Min, c.Max, c.Sum)
    90	}
    91	
    92	// Log outputs the stats to the logger.
    93	func (c *Counter) Log(msg string) {
    94	        log.Infof("%s : count %d avg %.8g +/- %.4g min %g max %g sum %.9g",
    95	                msg, c.Count, c.Avg(), c.StdDev(), c.Min, c.Max, c.Sum)
    96	}
    97	
    98	// Reset clears the counter to reset it to original 'no data' state.
    99	func (c *Counter) Reset() {
   100	        var empty Counter
   101	        *c = empty
   102	}
   103	
   104	// Transfer merges the data from src into this Counter and clears src.
   105	func (c *Counter) Transfer(src *Counter) {
   106	        if src.Count == 0 {
   107	                return // nothing to do
   108	        }
   109	        if c.Count == 0 {
   110	                *c = *src // copy everything at once
   111	                src.Reset()
   112	                return
   113	        }
   114	        c.Count += src.Count
   115	        if src.Min < c.Min {
   116	                c.Min = src.Min
   117	        }
   118	        if src.Max > c.Max {
   119	                c.Max = src.Max
   120	        }
   121	        c.Sum += src.Sum
   122	        c.sumOfSquares += src.sumOfSquares
   123	        src.Reset()
   124	}
   125	
   126	// Histogram - written in go with inspiration from https://github.com/facebook/wdt/blob/master/util/Stats.h
   127	
   128	// The intervals are [prev, current] so for "90" (previous is 80) the values in that bucket are >80 and <=90
   129	// that way a cumulative % up to that bucket means X% of the data <= 90 (or 100-X% > 90), works well for max too
   130	// There are 2 special buckets - the first one is from min to and including 0,
   131	// one after the last for value > last and up to max.
   132	var (
   133	        histogramBucketValues = []int32{
   134	                0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6,
   135	                7, 8, 9, 10, 11, // initially increment buckets by 1, my amp goes to 11 !
   136	                12, 14, 16, 18, 20, // then by 2
   137	                25, 30, 35, 40, 45, 50, // then by 5
   138	                60, 70, 80, 90, 100, // then by 10
   139	                120, 140, 160, 180, 200, // line3 *10
   140	                250, 300, 350, 400, 450, 500, // line4 *10
   141	                600, 700, 800, 900, 1000, // line5 *10
   142	                2000, 3000, 4000, 5000, 7500, 10000, // another order of magnitude coarsly covered
   143	                20000, 30000, 40000, 50000, 75000, 100000, // ditto, the end
   144	        }
   145	        numValues  = len(histogramBucketValues)
   146	        numBuckets = numValues + 1 // 1 special first bucket is <= 0; and 1 extra last bucket is > 100000
   147	        firstValue = float64(histogramBucketValues[0])
   148	        lastValue  = float64(histogramBucketValues[numValues-1])
   149	        val2Bucket []int // ends at 1000. Remaining values will not be received in constant time.
   150	
   151	        maxArrayValue      = int32(1000) // Last value looked up as O(1) array, the rest is linear search
   152	        maxArrayValueIndex = -1          // Index of maxArrayValue
   153	)
   154	
   155	// Histogram extends Counter and adds a histogram.
   156	// Must be created using NewHistogram or anotherHistogram.Clone()
   157	// and not directly.
   158	type Histogram struct {
   159	        Counter
   160	        Offset  float64 // offset applied to data before fitting into buckets
   161	        Divider float64 // divider applied to data before fitting into buckets
   162	        // Don't access directly (outside of this package):
   163	        Hdata []int32 // numValues buckets (one more than values, for last one)
   164	}
   165	
   166	// For export of the data:
   167	
   168	// Interval is a range from start to end.
   169	// Interval are left closed, open right expect the last one which includes Max.
   170	// i.e., [Start, End] with the next one being [PrevEnd, NextEnd].
   171	type Interval struct {
   172	        Start float64
   173	        End   float64
   174	}
   175	
   176	// Bucket is the data for 1 bucket: an Interval and the occurrence Count for
   177	// that interval.
   178	type Bucket struct {
   179	        Interval
   180	        Percent float64 // Cumulative percentile
   181	        Count   int64   // How many in this bucket
   182	}
   183	
   184	// Percentile value for the percentile.
   185	type Percentile struct {
   186	        Percentile float64 // For this Percentile
   187	        Value      float64 // value at that Percentile
   188	}
   189	
   190	// HistogramData is the exported Histogram data, a sorted list of intervals
   191	// covering [Min, Max]. Pure data, so Counter for instance is flattened.
   192	type HistogramData struct {
   193	        Count       int64
   194	        Min         float64
   195	        Max         float64
   196	        Sum         float64
   197	        Avg         float64
   198	        StdDev      float64
   199	        Data        []Bucket
   200	        Percentiles []Percentile `json:"Percentiles,omitempty"`
   201	}
   202	
   203	// NewHistogram creates a new histogram (sets up the buckets).
   204	// Divider value can not be zero, otherwise returns zero.
   205	func NewHistogram(offset float64, divider float64) *Histogram {
   206	        if divider == 0 {
   207	                return nil
   208	        }
   209	        h := Histogram{
   210	                Offset:  offset,
   211	                Divider: divider,
   212	                Hdata:   make([]int32, numBuckets),
   213	        }
   214	        return &h
   215	}
   216	
   217	// Val2Bucket values are kept in two different structure
   218	// val2Bucket allows you reach between 0 and 1000 in constant time.
   219	//
   220	//nolint:gochecknoinits // we need to init these.
   221	func init() {
   222	        val2Bucket = make([]int, maxArrayValue)
   223	        maxArrayValueIndex = -1
   224	        for i, value := range histogramBucketValues {
   225	                if value == maxArrayValue {
   226	                        maxArrayValueIndex = i
   227	                        break
   228	                }
   229	        }
   230	        if maxArrayValueIndex == -1 {
   231	                log.Fatalf("Bug boundary maxArrayValue=%d not found in bucket list %v", maxArrayValue, histogramBucketValues)
   232	        }
   233	        idx := 0
   234	        for i := range maxArrayValue {
   235	                if i >= histogramBucketValues[idx] {
   236	                        idx++
   237	                }
   238	                val2Bucket[i] = idx
   239	        }
   240	        // coding bug detection (aka impossible if it works once) until 1000
   241	        if idx != maxArrayValueIndex {
   242	                log.Fatalf("Bug in creating histogram index idx %d vs index %d up to %d", idx, int(maxArrayValue), maxArrayValue)
   243	        }
   244	}
   245	
   246	// lookUpIdx looks for scaledValue's index in histogramBucketValues
   247	// TODO: change linear time to O(log(N)) with binary search.
   248	func lookUpIdx(scaledValue int) int {
   249	        scaledValue32 := int32(scaledValue) //nolint:gosec // we limit ourselves to 32 bits counts.
   250	        if scaledValue32 < maxArrayValue {  // constant
   251	                return val2Bucket[scaledValue]
   252	        }
   253	        for i := maxArrayValueIndex; i < numValues; i++ {
   254	                if histogramBucketValues[i] > scaledValue32 {
   255	                        return i
   256	                }
   257	        }
   258	        log.Fatalf("never reached/bug")
   259	        return 0
   260	}
   261	
   262	// Record records a data point.
   263	func (h *Histogram) Record(v float64) {
   264	        h.RecordN(v, 1)
   265	}
   266	
   267	// RecordN efficiently records a data point N times.
   268	func (h *Histogram) RecordN(v float64, n int) {
   269	        h.Counter.RecordN(v, n)
   270	        h.record(v, n)
   271	}
   272	
   273	// Records v value to count times.
   274	func (h *Histogram) record(v float64, count int) {
   275	        // Scaled value to bucketize - we used to subtract epsilon because the interval
   276	        // is open to the left ] start, end ] so when exactly on start it has
   277	        // to fall on the previous bucket: which is more correctly done using
   278	        // math.Ceil()-1 but that doesn't work... so back to epsilon distance.
   279	        scaledVal := (v - h.Offset) / h.Divider
   280	        var idx int
   281	        switch {
   282	        case scaledVal <= firstValue:
   283	                idx = 0
   284	        case scaledVal > lastValue:
   285	                idx = numBuckets - 1 // last bucket is for > last value
   286	        default:
   287	                // else we look it up (with the open interval adjustment)
   288	                svInt := int(scaledVal)
   289	                delta := scaledVal - float64(svInt)
   290	                if delta < 1e-12 {
   291	                        svInt--
   292	                }
   293	                log.Debugf("v %f -> scaledVal %.17f ceil %f delta %g - svInt %d", v, scaledVal, math.Ceil(scaledVal), delta, svInt)
   294	                idx = lookUpIdx(svInt)
   295	        }
   296	        h.Hdata[idx] += int32(count) //nolint:gosec // we limit ourselves to 32 bits counts.
   297	}
   298	
   299	// CalcPercentile returns the value for an input percentile
   300	// e.g., for 90. as input returns an estimate of the original value threshold
   301	// where 90.0% of the data is below said threshold.
   302	// with 3 data points 10, 20, 30; p0-p33.33 == 10, p 66.666 = 20, p100 = 30
   303	// p33.333 - p66.666 = linear between 10 and 20; so p50 = 15
   304	// TODO: consider spreading the count of the bucket evenly from start to end
   305	// so the % grows by at least to 1/N on start of range, and for last range
   306	// when start == end we should get to that % faster.
   307	func (e *HistogramData) CalcPercentile(percentile float64) float64 {
   308	        if len(e.Data) == 0 {
   309	                log.Errf("Unexpected call to CalcPercentile(%g) with no data", percentile)
   310	                return 0
   311	        }
   312	        if percentile >= 100 {
   313	                return e.Max
   314	        }
   315	        // We assume Min is at least a single point so at least covers 1/Count %
   316	        pp := 100. / float64(e.Count) // previous percentile
   317	        if percentile <= pp {
   318	                return e.Min
   319	        }
   320	        for i := range e.Data {
   321	                cur := &e.Data[i]
   322	                if percentile <= cur.Percent {
   323	                        return cur.Start + (percentile-pp)/(cur.Percent-pp)*(cur.End-cur.Start)
   324	                }
   325	                pp = cur.Percent
   326	        }
   327	        return e.Max // not reached
   328	}
   329	
   330	// Export translate the internal representation of the histogram data in
   331	// an externally usable one. Calculates the request Percentiles.
   332	func (h *Histogram) Export() *HistogramData {
   333	        var res HistogramData
   334	        res.Count = h.Counter.Count
   335	        res.Min = h.Counter.Min
   336	        res.Max = h.Counter.Max
   337	        res.Sum = h.Counter.Sum
   338	        res.Avg = h.Counter.Avg()
   339	        res.StdDev = h.Counter.StdDev()
   340	        multiplier := h.Divider
   341	        offset := h.Offset
   342	        // calculate the last bucket index
   343	        lastIdx := -1
   344	        for i := numBuckets - 1; i >= 0; i-- {
   345	                if h.Hdata[i] > 0 {
   346	                        lastIdx = i
   347	                        break
   348	                }
   349	        }
   350	        if lastIdx == -1 {
   351	                return &res
   352	        }
   353	
   354	        // previous bucket value:
   355	        prev := histogramBucketValues[0]
   356	        var total int64
   357	        ctrTotal := float64(h.Count)
   358	        // export the data of each bucket of the histogram
   359	        for i := 0; i <= lastIdx; i++ {
   360	                if h.Hdata[i] == 0 {
   361	                        // empty bucket: skip it, but update prev which is needed for next iteration
   362	                        if i < numValues {
   363	                                prev = histogramBucketValues[i]
   364	                        }
   365	                        continue
   366	                }
   367	                var b Bucket
   368	                total += int64(h.Hdata[i])
   369	                if len(res.Data) == 0 {
   370	                        // First entry, start is min
   371	                        b.Start = h.Min
   372	                } else {
   373	                        b.Start = multiplier*float64(prev) + offset
   374	                }
   375	                b.Percent = 100. * float64(total) / ctrTotal
   376	                if i < numValues {
   377	                        cur := histogramBucketValues[i]
   378	                        b.End = multiplier*float64(cur) + offset
   379	                        prev = cur
   380	                } else {
   381	                        // Last Entry
   382	                        b.Start = multiplier*float64(prev) + offset
   383	                        b.End = h.Max
   384	                }
   385	                b.Count = int64(h.Hdata[i])
   386	                res.Data = append(res.Data, b)
   387	        }
   388	        res.Data[len(res.Data)-1].End = h.Max
   389	        return &res
   390	}
   391	
   392	// CalcPercentiles calculates the requested percentile and adds them to the
   393	// HistogramData. Potential TODO: sort or assume sorting and calculate all
   394	// the percentiles in 1 pass (greater and greater values).
   395	func (e *HistogramData) CalcPercentiles(percentiles []float64) *HistogramData {
   396	        if e.Count == 0 {
   397	                return e
   398	        }
   399	        for _, p := range percentiles {
   400	                e.Percentiles = append(e.Percentiles, Percentile{p, e.CalcPercentile(p)})
   401	        }
   402	        return e
   403	}
   404	
   405	// Print dumps the histogram (and counter) to the provided writer.
   406	// Also calculates the percentile.
   407	func (e *HistogramData) Print(out io.Writer, msg string) {
   408	        if len(e.Data) == 0 {
   409	                _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "%s : no data\n", msg)
   410	                return
   411	        }
   412	        // the base counterpart:
   413	        _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "%s : count %d avg %.8g +/- %.4g min %g max %g sum %.9g\n",
   414	                msg, e.Count, e.Avg, e.StdDev, e.Min, e.Max, e.Sum)
   415	        _, _ = fmt.Fprintln(out, "# range, mid point, percentile, count")
   416	        sep := ">="
   417	        for i := range e.Data {
   418	                b := &e.Data[i]
   419	                if i > 0 {
   420	                        sep = ">" // last interval is inclusive (of max value)
   421	                }
   422	                _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "%s %.6g <= %.6g , %.6g , %.2f, %d\n", sep, b.Start, b.End, (b.Start+b.End)/2., b.Percent, b.Count)
   423	        }
   424	        // print the information of target percentiles
   425	        for _, p := range e.Percentiles {
   426	                _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "# target %g%% %.6g\n", p.Percentile, p.Value)
   427	        }
   428	}
   429	
   430	// Print dumps the histogram (and counter) to the provided writer.
   431	// Also calculates the percentiles. Use Export() once and Print if you
   432	// are going to need the Export results too.
   433	func (h *Histogram) Print(out io.Writer, msg string, percentiles []float64) {
   434	        h.Export().CalcPercentiles(percentiles).Print(out, msg)
   435	}
   436	
   437	// Log Logs the histogram to the counter.
   438	func (h *Histogram) Log(msg string, percentiles []float64) {
   439	        var b bytes.Buffer
   440	        w := bufio.NewWriter(&b)
   441	        h.Print(w, msg, percentiles)
   442	        _ = w.Flush()
   443	        log.Infof("%s", b.Bytes())
   444	}
   445	
   446	// Reset clears the data. Reset it to NewHistogram state.
   447	func (h *Histogram) Reset() {
   448	        h.Counter.Reset()
   449	        // Leave Offset and Divider alone
   450	        for i := 0; i < len(h.Hdata); i++ {
   451	                h.Hdata[i] = 0
   452	        }
   453	}
   454	
   455	// Clone returns a copy of the histogram.
   456	func (h *Histogram) Clone() *Histogram {
   457	        hCopy := NewHistogram(h.Offset, h.Divider)
   458	        hCopy.CopyFrom(h)
   459	        return hCopy
   460	}
   461	
   462	// CopyFrom sets the content of this object to a copy of the src.
   463	func (h *Histogram) CopyFrom(src *Histogram) {
   464	        h.Counter = src.Counter
   465	        h.copyHDataFrom(src)
   466	}
   467	
   468	// copyHDataFrom appends histogram data values to this object from the src.
   469	// Src histogram data values will be appended according to this object's
   470	// offset and divider.
   471	func (h *Histogram) copyHDataFrom(src *Histogram) {
   472	        if h.Divider == src.Divider && h.Offset == src.Offset {
   473	                for i := 0; i < len(h.Hdata); i++ {
   474	                        h.Hdata[i] += src.Hdata[i]
   475	                }
   476	                return
   477	        }
   478	        hData := src.Export()
   479	        for i := range hData.Data {
   480	                data := hData.Data[i]
   481	                h.record((data.Start+data.End)/2, int(data.Count))
   482	        }
   483	}
   484	
   485	// Merge two different histogram with different scale parameters
   486	// Lowest offset and highest divider value will be selected on new Histogram as scale parameters.
   487	func Merge(h1 *Histogram, h2 *Histogram) *Histogram {
   488	        divider := h1.Divider
   489	        offset := h1.Offset
   490	        if h2.Divider > h1.Divider {
   491	                divider = h2.Divider
   492	        }
   493	        if h2.Offset < h1.Offset {
   494	                offset = h2.Offset
   495	        }
   496	        newH := NewHistogram(offset, divider)
   497	        newH.Transfer(h1)
   498	        newH.Transfer(h2)
   499	        return newH
   500	}
   501	
   502	// Transfer merges the data from src into this Histogram and clears src.
   503	func (h *Histogram) Transfer(src *Histogram) {
   504	        if src.Count == 0 {
   505	                return
   506	        }
   507	        if h.Count == 0 {
   508	                h.CopyFrom(src)
   509	                src.Reset()
   510	                return
   511	        }
   512	        h.copyHDataFrom(src)
   513	        h.Counter.Transfer(&src.Counter)
   514	        src.Reset()
   515	}
   516	
   517	// ParsePercentiles extracts the percentiles from string (flag).
   518	func ParsePercentiles(percentiles string) ([]float64, error) {
   519	        percs := strings.Split(percentiles, ",") // will make a size 1 array for empty input!
   520	        res := make([]float64, 0, len(percs))
   521	        for _, pStr := range percs {
   522	                pStr = strings.TrimSpace(pStr)
   523	                if len(pStr) == 0 {
   524	                        continue
   525	                }
   526	                p, err := strconv.ParseFloat(pStr, 64)
   527	                if err != nil {
   528	                        return res, err
   529	                }
   530	                if p <= 0 || p >= 100 {
   531	                        return res, fmt.Errorf("percentile %g must be > 0 and < 100", p)
   532	                }
   533	                res = append(res, p)
   534	        }
   535	        if len(res) == 0 {
   536	                return res, errors.New("list can't be empty")
   537	        }
   538	        log.LogVf("Will use %v for percentiles", res)
   539	        return res, nil
   540	}

    99	// SharedMain is the common part of main from fortio_main and fcurl.
   100	// It sets up the common flags, the rest of usage/argument/flag handling
   101	// is now moved to the [fortio.org/cli] and [fortio.org/scli] packages.
   102	func SharedMain() {
   103	        flag.Func("H",
   104	                "Additional HTTP header(s) or gRPC metadata. Multiple `key:value` pairs can be passed using multiple -H.",
   105	                httpOpts.AddAndValidateExtraHeader)
   106	        flag.IntVar(&fhttp.BufferSizeKb, "httpbufferkb", fhttp.BufferSizeKb,
   107	                "Size of the buffer (max data size) for the optimized HTTP client in `kbytes`")
   108	        flag.BoolVar(&fhttp.CheckConnectionClosedHeader, "httpccch", fhttp.CheckConnectionClosedHeader,
   109	                "Check for Connection: Close Header")
   110	        // FlagResolveIPType indicates which IP types to resolve.
   111	        // With round-robin resolution now the default, you are likely to get IPv6 which may not work if
   112	        // use both type (`ip`). In particular some test environments like the CI do have IPv6
   113	        // for localhost but fail to connect. So we made the default ip4 only.
   114	        dflag.Flag("resolve-ip-type", fnet.FlagResolveIPType)
   115	        // FlagResolveMethod decides which method to use when multiple IPs are returned for a given name
   116	        // default assumes one gets all the IPs in the first call and does round-robin across these.
   117	        // first just picks the first answer, rr rounds robin on each answer.
   118	        dflag.Flag("dns-method", fnet.FlagResolveMethod)
   119	        dflag.Flag("echo-server-default-params", fhttp.DefaultEchoServerParams)
   120	        dflag.FlagBool("proxy-all-headers", fhttp.Fetch2CopiesAllHeader)
   121	        dflag.Flag("server-idle-timeout", fhttp.ServerIdleTimeout)
   122	        // MaxDelay is the maximum delay allowed for the echoserver responses.
   123	        // It is a dynamic flag with default value of 1.5s so we can test the default 1s timeout in envoy.
   124	        dflag.Flag("max-echo-delay", fhttp.MaxDelay)
   125	        // call [scli.ServerMain()] to complete the setup.
   126	}
   127	
   128	// FetchURL is fetching url content and exiting with 1 upon error.
   129	// common part between fortio_main and fcurl.
   130	func FetchURL(o *fhttp.HTTPOptions) {
   131	        // keepAlive could be just false when making 1 fetch, but it helps debugging
   132	        // the HTTP client when making a single request if using the flags
   133	        o.DataWriter = os.Stdout
   134	        client, _ := fhttp.NewClient(o)
   135	        // big gotcha that nil client isn't nil interface value (!)
   136	        if client == nil || reflect.ValueOf(client).IsNil() {
   137	                os.Exit(1) // error logged already
   138	        }
   139	        var code int
   140	        var dataLen int64
   141	        var header uint
   142	        if client.HasBuffer() {
   143	                // Fast client
   144	                var data []byte
   145	                var headerI int
   146	                code, data, headerI = client.Fetch(context.Background())
   147	                dataLen = safecast.MustConvert[int64](len(data))
   148	                header = safecast.MustConvert[uint](headerI)
   149	                if *curlHeadersStdout {
   150	                        os.Stdout.Write(data)
   151	                } else {
   152	                        os.Stderr.Write(data[:header])
   153	                        os.Stdout.Write(data[header:])
   154	                }
   155	        } else {
   156	                code, dataLen, header = client.StreamFetch(context.Background())
   157	        }
   158	        log.LogVf("Fetch result code %d, data len %d, headerlen %d", code, dataLen, header)
   159	        if code != http.StatusOK {
   160	                log.Errf("Error status %d", code)
   161	                os.Exit(1)
   162	        }
   163	}
   164	
   165	// TLSInsecure returns true if -k or -https-insecure was passed.
   166	func TLSInsecure() bool {
   167	        TLSInsecure := *httpsInsecureFlag || *httpsInsecureFlagL
   168	        if TLSInsecure {
   169	                log.Infof("TLS certificates will not be verified, per flag request")
   170	        } else {
   171	                log.LogVf("Will verify TLS certificates, use -k / -https-insecure to disable")
   172	        }
   173	        return TLSInsecure
   174	}
   175	
   176	// ConnectionReuseRangeValidator returns a validator function that checks if the connection reuse range is valid
   177	// and set in httpOpts.
   178	func ConnectionReuseRangeValidator(httpOpts *fhttp.HTTPOptions) func(string) error {
   179	        return func(value string) error {
   180	                return httpOpts.ValidateAndSetConnectionReuseRange(value)
   181	        }
   182	}
   183	
   184	// SharedHTTPOptions is the flag->httpoptions transfer code shared between
   185	// fortio_main and fcurl. It also sets fhttp.DefaultHTTPOptions.
   186	func SharedHTTPOptions() *fhttp.HTTPOptions {
   187	        url := strings.TrimLeft(flag.Arg(0), " \t\r\n")
   188	        httpOpts.URL = url
   189	        httpOpts.HTTP10 = *http10Flag
   190	        httpOpts.H2 = *h2Flag
   191	        httpOpts.DisableFastClient = *stdClientFlag
   192	        httpOpts.DisableKeepAlive = !*keepAliveFlag
   193	        httpOpts.AllowHalfClose = *halfCloseFlag
   194	        httpOpts.Compression = *compressionFlag
   195	        httpOpts.HTTPReqTimeOut = *httpReqTimeoutFlag
   196	        httpOpts.Insecure = TLSInsecure()
   197	        httpOpts.Resolve = *resolve
   198	        httpOpts.UserCredentials = *userCredentialsFlag
   199	        if len(*contentTypeFlag) > 0 {
   200	                // only set content-type from flag if flag isn't empty as it can come also from -H content-type:...
   201	                httpOpts.ContentType = *contentTypeFlag
   202	        }
   203	        if *PayloadStreamFlag {
   204	                httpOpts.PayloadReader = os.Stdin
   205	        } else {
   206	                // Returns nil if file read error, an empty but non nil slice if no payload is requested.
   207	                httpOpts.Payload = fnet.GeneratePayload(*PayloadFileFlag, *PayloadSizeFlag, *PayloadFlag)
   208	                if httpOpts.Payload == nil {
   209	                        // Error already logged
   210	                        os.Exit(1)
   211	                }
   212	        }
   213	        httpOpts.UnixDomainSocket = *unixDomainSocketFlag
   214	        if *followRedirectsFlag {
   215	                httpOpts.FollowRedirects = true
   216	                httpOpts.DisableFastClient = true
   217	        }
   218	        httpOpts.CACert = *CACertFlag
   219	        httpOpts.Cert = *CertFlag
   220	        httpOpts.Key = *KeyFlag
   221	        httpOpts.MTLS = *mTLS
   222	        httpOpts.LogErrors = *LogErrorsFlag
   223	        httpOpts.SequentialWarmup = *warmupFlag
   224	        httpOpts.NoResolveEachConn = *NoReResolveFlag
   225	        httpOpts.MethodOverride = *MethodFlag
   226	        fhttp.DefaultHTTPOptions = &httpOpts
   227	        return &httpOpts
   228	}

    15	// Package periodic for fortio (from greek for load) is a set of utilities to
    16	// run a given task at a target rate (qps) and gather statistics - for instance
    17	// HTTP requests.
    18	//
    19	// The main executable using the library is fortio, but there
    20	// is also ../histogram to use the stats from the command line and ../echosrv
    21	// as a very light HTTP server that can be used to test proxies etc like
    22	// the Istio components.
    23	package periodic // import "fortio.org/fortio/periodic"

    43	// DefaultRunnerOptions are the default values for options (do not mutate!).
    44	// This is only useful for initializing flag default values.
    45	// You do not need to use this directly, you can pass a newly created
    46	// RunnerOptions and 0 valued fields will be reset to these defaults.
    47	var DefaultRunnerOptions = RunnerOptions{
    48	        QPS:         8,
    49	        Duration:    5 * time.Second,
    50	        NumThreads:  4,
    51	        Percentiles: []float64{90.0},
    52	        Resolution:  0.001, // milliseconds
    53	}

    55	type ThreadID int
    56	
    57	// Runnable are the function to run periodically.
    58	type Runnable interface {
    59	        // Run returns a boolean, true for normal/success, false otherwise.
    60	        // with details being an optional string that can be put in the access logs.
    61	        // Statistics are split into two sets.
    62	        Run(ctx context.Context, id ThreadID) (status bool, details string)
    63	}
    64	
    65	// MakeRunners creates an array of NumThreads identical Runnable instances
    66	// (for the (rare/test) cases where there is no unique state needed).
    67	func (r *RunnerOptions) MakeRunners(rr Runnable) {
    68	        log.Infof("Making %d clone of %+v", r.NumThreads, rr)
    69	        if len(r.Runners) < r.NumThreads {
    70	                log.Infof("Resizing runners from %d to %d", len(r.Runners), r.NumThreads)
    71	                r.Runners = make([]Runnable, r.NumThreads)
    72	        }
    73	        for i := range r.NumThreads {
    74	                r.Runners[i] = rr
    75	        }
    76	}
    77	
    78	// ReleaseRunners clear the runners state.
    79	func (r *RunnerOptions) ReleaseRunners() {
    80	        for idx := range r.Runners {
    81	                r.Runners[idx] = nil
    82	        }
    83	}
    84	
    85	// Aborter is the object controlling Abort() of the runs.
    86	type Aborter struct {
    87	        sync.Mutex
    88	        StopChan      chan struct{}
    89	        StartChan     chan bool // Used to signal actual start of the run. Also (re)used in rapi/ to signal completion of the Run().
    90	        hasStarted    bool
    91	        stopRequested bool
    92	}
    93	
    94	// Note this can cause data race if called without holding the lock. TODO: maybe use reentrant lock. but this is for debug only.
    95	func (a *Aborter) String() string {
    96	        return fmt.Sprintf("{Aborter %p stopChan %v startChan %v hasStarted %v stopRequested %v}",
    97	                a, a.StopChan, a.StartChan, a.hasStarted, a.stopRequested)
    98	}
    99	
   100	// Abort signals all the go routine of this run to stop.
   101	// Implemented by closing the shared channel. The lock is to make sure
   102	// we close it exactly once to avoid go panic.
   103	// If wait is true, waits for the run to be started before closing.
   104	func (a *Aborter) Abort(wait bool) {
   105	        a.Lock()
   106	        if a.StopChan == nil {
   107	                // Already done
   108	                log.LogVf("ABORT already aborted %v", a)
   109	                a.Unlock()
   110	                return
   111	        }
   112	        a.stopRequested = true
   113	        started := a.hasStarted
   114	        if started || !wait {
   115	                log.LogVf("ABORT Closing already started or not waiting %v", a)
   116	                close(a.StopChan)
   117	                a.StopChan = nil
   118	                a.Unlock()
   119	                if started {
   120	                        log.LogVf("ABORT reading start channel")
   121	                        // shouldn't block/hang, just purging/resetting - but another aborter (line 137 might have consumed it already)
   122	                        select {
   123	                        case b := <-a.StartChan:
   124	                                log.LogVf("ABORT done reading start channel, got %v", b)
   125	                        default:
   126	                                log.LogVf("ABORT start channel empty (not quite expected)")
   127	                        }
   128	                        a.Lock()
   129	                        a.hasStarted = false
   130	                        a.Unlock()
   131	                }
   132	                return
   133	        }
   134	        // Wait & not started case:
   135	        a.Unlock()
   136	        log.LogVf("ABORT Waiting for start")
   137	        b := <-a.StartChan
   138	        log.LogVf("ABORT Done waiting for start, got %v", b)
   139	        a.Lock()
   140	        if a.StopChan != nil {
   141	                log.LogVf("ABORT Closing wasn't started %+v", a)
   142	                close(a.StopChan)
   143	                a.StopChan = nil
   144	        }
   145	        a.hasStarted = false
   146	        a.Unlock()
   147	}
   148	
   149	// RecordStart records the start of the run. (used by httprunner in error cases to fake start so rapi stop and wait can work).
   150	func (a *Aborter) RecordStart() (chan struct{}, bool) {
   151	        a.Lock()
   152	        a.hasStarted = true
   153	        startedChan := a.StartChan
   154	        runnerChan := a.StopChan // need a copy to not race with assignment to nil
   155	        shouldAbort := a.stopRequested
   156	        log.LogVf("RUNNER starting... can now be Abort()ed, telling %v - %v", a, startedChan)
   157	        a.Unlock()
   158	        startedChan <- true
   159	        return runnerChan, shouldAbort
   160	}
   161	
   162	// Reset returns the aborter to original state, for (unit test) reuse.
   163	// Note that it doesn't recreate the closed stop chan.
   164	func (a *Aborter) Reset() {
   165	        a.Lock()
   166	        // Clear the "started" if we would get reused
   167	        select {
   168	        case <-a.StartChan:
   169	                log.LogVf("RUNNER reset: Started chan flushed for reuse")
   170	        default:
   171	                log.LogVf("RUNNER reset: we were Abort()ed already, start chan empty")
   172	        }
   173	        a.hasStarted = false
   174	        a.stopRequested = false
   175	        a.Unlock()
   176	}
   177	
   178	// NewAborter makes a new Aborter and initialize its StopChan.
   179	// The pointer should be shared. The structure is NoCopy.
   180	func NewAborter() *Aborter {
   181	        res := &Aborter{StopChan: make(chan struct{}, 1), StartChan: make(chan bool, 1)}
   182	        log.LogVf("NewAborter called %p %+v", res, res)
   183	        return res
   184	}

   186	// RunnerOptions are the parameters to the PeriodicRunner.
   187	type RunnerOptions struct {
   188	        // Type of run (to be copied into results)
   189	        RunType string
   190	        // Array of objects to run in each thread (use MakeRunners() to clone the same one)
   191	        Runners []Runnable `json:"-"`
   192	        // At which (target) rate to run the Runners across NumThreads.
   193	        QPS float64
   194	        // How long to run the test for. Unless Exactly is specified.
   195	        Duration time.Duration
   196	        // Note that this actually maps to gorountines and not actual threads,
   197	        // but threads seems like a more familiar name to use for non go users
   198	        // and in a benchmarking context
   199	        NumThreads int
   200	        // List of percentiles to calculate.
   201	        Percentiles []float64
   202	        // Divider to apply to duration data in seconds. Defaults to 0.001 or 1 millisecond.
   203	        Resolution float64
   204	        // Where to write the textual version of the results, defaults to stdout
   205	        Out io.Writer `json:"-"`
   206	        // Extra data to be copied back to the results (to be saved/JSON serialized)
   207	        Labels string
   208	        // Aborter to interrupt a run. Will be created if not set/left nil. Or you
   209	        // can pass your own. It is very important this is a pointer and not a field
   210	        // as RunnerOptions themselves get copied while the channel and lock must
   211	        // stay unique (per run).
   212	        Stop *Aborter `json:"-"`
   213	        // Mode where an exact number of iterations is requested. Default (0) is
   214	        // to not use that mode. If specified Duration is not used.
   215	        Exactly int64
   216	        // When multiple clients are used to generate requests, they tend to send
   217	        // requests very close to one another, causing a thundering herd problem
   218	        // Enabling jitter (+/-10%) allows these requests to be de-synchronized
   219	        // When enabled, it is only effective in the '-qps' mode.
   220	        Jitter bool
   221	        // When multiple clients are used to generate requests, they tend to send
   222	        // requests very close to one another, causing a thundering herd problem
   223	        // Enabling uniform causes the requests between connections to be uniformly staggered.
   224	        // When enabled, it is only effective in the '-qps' mode.
   225	        Uniform bool
   226	        // Optional run id; used by the server to identify runs.
   227	        RunID int64
   228	        // Optional Offset Duration; to offset the histogram function duration
   229	        Offset time.Duration
   230	        // Optional AccessLogger to log every request made. See AddAccessLogger.
   231	        AccessLogger AccessLogger `json:"-"`
   232	        // No catch-up: if true we will do exactly the requested QPS and not try to catch up if the target is temporarily slow.
   233	        NoCatchUp bool
   234	        // Unique 96 character ID used as reference to saved JSON file. Created during Normalize().
   235	        ID string
   236	        // Time the object got first normalized, used to generate the unique ID above.
   237	        genTime *time.Time
   238	}
   239	
   240	// RunnerResults encapsulates the actual QPS observed and duration histogram.
   241	type RunnerResults struct {
   242	        RunType           string
   243	        Labels            string
   244	        StartTime         time.Time
   245	        RequestedQPS      string
   246	        RequestedDuration string // String version of the requested duration or exact count
   247	        ActualQPS         float64
   248	        ActualDuration    time.Duration
   249	        NumThreads        int
   250	        Version           string
   251	        // DurationHistogram all the Run. If you want to exclude the error cases; subtract ErrorsDurationHistogram to each bucket.
   252	        DurationHistogram *stats.HistogramData
   253	        // ErrorsDurationHistogram is the durations of the error (Run returning false) cases.
   254	        ErrorsDurationHistogram *stats.HistogramData
   255	        Exactly                 int64 // Echo back the requested count
   256	        Jitter                  bool
   257	        Uniform                 bool
   258	        NoCatchUp               bool
   259	        RunID                   int64 // Echo back the optional run id
   260	        AccessLoggerInfo        string
   261	        // Same as RunnerOptions ID:  Unique 96 character ID used as reference to saved JSON file. Created during Normalize().
   262	        ID string
   263	        // If the run doesn't even start because of for instance an invalid host name, this will be set (all omitted on success)
   264	        jrpc.ServerReply
   265	}

   267	// HasRunnerResult is the interface implicitly implemented by HTTPRunnerResults
   268	// and GrpcRunnerResults, so the common results can be extracted irrespective
   269	// of the type.
   270	type HasRunnerResult interface {
   271	        Result() *RunnerResults
   272	}
   273	
   274	// Result returns the common RunnerResults.
   275	func (r *RunnerResults) Result() *RunnerResults {
   276	        return r
   277	}
   278	
   279	// PeriodicRunner let's you exercise the Function at the given QPS and collect
   280	// statistics and histogram about the run.
   281	type PeriodicRunner interface { //nolint:revive // stutter is ok for this (can't break api anyway).
   282	        // Starts the run. Returns actual QPS and Histogram of function durations.
   283	        Run() RunnerResults
   284	        // Returns the options normalized by constructor - do not mutate
   285	        // (where is const when you need it...)
   286	        Options() *RunnerOptions
   287	}
   288	
   289	// Unexposed implementation details for PeriodicRunner.
   290	type periodicRunner struct {
   291	        RunnerOptions
   292	}
   293	
   294	var (
   295	        gAbortChan       chan os.Signal
   296	        gOutstandingRuns int64
   297	        gAbortMutex      sync.Mutex
   298	)
   299	
   300	// Normalize initializes and normalizes the runner options. In particular it sets
   301	// up the channel that can be used to interrupt the run later.
   302	// Once Normalize is called, if Run() is skipped, Abort() must be called to
   303	// cleanup the watchers.
   304	func (r *RunnerOptions) Normalize() {
   305	        if r.QPS == 0 {
   306	                r.QPS = DefaultRunnerOptions.QPS
   307	        } else if r.QPS < 0 {
   308	                log.LogVf("Negative qps %f means max speed mode/no wait between calls", r.QPS)
   309	                r.QPS = -1
   310	        }
   311	        if r.Out == nil {
   312	                r.Out = os.Stdout
   313	        }
   314	        if r.NumThreads == 0 {
   315	                r.NumThreads = DefaultRunnerOptions.NumThreads
   316	        }
   317	        if r.NumThreads < 1 {
   318	                r.NumThreads = 1
   319	        }
   320	        if r.Percentiles == nil {
   321	                r.Percentiles = make([]float64, len(DefaultRunnerOptions.Percentiles))
   322	                copy(r.Percentiles, DefaultRunnerOptions.Percentiles)
   323	        }
   324	        if r.Resolution <= 0 {
   325	                r.Resolution = DefaultRunnerOptions.Resolution
   326	        }
   327	        if r.Duration == 0 {
   328	                r.Duration = DefaultRunnerOptions.Duration
   329	        }
   330	        if r.Runners == nil {
   331	                r.Runners = make([]Runnable, r.NumThreads)
   332	        }
   333	        if r.ID == "" {
   334	                r.GenID()
   335	        }
   336	        if r.Stop != nil {
   337	                return
   338	        }
   339	        // nil aborter (last normalization step:)
   340	        r.Stop = NewAborter()
   341	        runnerChan := r.Stop.StopChan // need a copy to not race with assignment to nil
   342	        go func() {
   343	                gAbortMutex.Lock()
   344	                gOutstandingRuns++
   345	                n := gOutstandingRuns
   346	                if gAbortChan == nil {
   347	                        log.LogVf("WATCHER %d First outstanding run starting, catching signal", n)
   348	                        gAbortChan = make(chan os.Signal, 1)
   349	                        signal.Notify(gAbortChan, os.Interrupt)
   350	                }
   351	                abortChan := gAbortChan
   352	                gAbortMutex.Unlock()
   353	                log.LogVf("WATCHER %d starting new watcher for signal! chan  g %v r %v (%d)", n, abortChan, runnerChan, runtime.NumGoroutine())
   354	                select {
   355	                case _, ok := <-abortChan:
   356	                        log.LogVf("WATCHER %d got interrupt signal! %v", n, ok)
   357	                        if ok {
   358	                                gAbortMutex.Lock()
   359	                                if gAbortChan != nil {
   360	                                        log.LogVf("WATCHER %d closing %v to notify all", n, gAbortChan)
   361	                                        close(gAbortChan)
   362	                                        gAbortChan = nil
   363	                                }
   364	                                gAbortMutex.Unlock()
   365	                        }
   366	                        r.Abort()
   367	                case <-runnerChan:
   368	                        log.LogVf("WATCHER %d r.Stop readable", n)
   369	                        // nothing to do, stop happened
   370	                }
   371	                log.LogVf("WATCHER %d End of go routine", n)
   372	                gAbortMutex.Lock()
   373	                gOutstandingRuns--
   374	                if gOutstandingRuns == 0 {
   375	                        log.LogVf("WATCHER %d Last watcher: resetting signal handler", n)
   376	                        gAbortChan = nil
   377	                        signal.Reset(os.Interrupt)
   378	                } else {
   379	                        log.LogVf("WATCHER %d isn't the last one, %d left", n, gOutstandingRuns)
   380	                }
   381	                gAbortMutex.Unlock()
   382	        }()
   383	}
   384	
   385	// Abort safely aborts the run by closing the channel and resetting that channel
   386	// to nil under lock so it can be called multiple times and not create panic for
   387	// already closed channel.
   388	func (r *RunnerOptions) Abort() {
   389	        log.LogVf("Abort called for %p", r)
   390	        if r.Stop != nil {
   391	                r.Stop.Abort(false)
   392	        }
   393	}
   394	
   395	// internal version, returning the concrete implementation. logical std::move.
   396	func newPeriodicRunner(opts *RunnerOptions) *periodicRunner {
   397	        r := &periodicRunner{*opts} // by default just copy the input params
   398	        opts.ReleaseRunners()
   399	        opts.Stop = nil
   400	        opts.genTime = nil
   401	        r.Normalize()
   402	        return r
   403	}
   404	
   405	// NewPeriodicRunner constructs a runner from input parameters/options.
   406	// The options will be moved and normalized to the returned object, do
   407	// not use the original options after this call, call Options() instead.
   408	// Abort() must be called if Run() is not called.
   409	// You can also keep a pointer to the original Aborter and use it, if needed.
   410	func NewPeriodicRunner(params *RunnerOptions) PeriodicRunner {
   411	        return newPeriodicRunner(params)
   412	}
   413	
   414	// Options returns the options pointer.
   415	func (r *periodicRunner) Options() *RunnerOptions {
   416	        return &r.RunnerOptions // sort of returning this here
   417	}
   418	
   419	func (r *periodicRunner) runQPSSetup(extra string) (requestedDuration string, requestedQPS string, numCalls int64, leftOver int64) {
   420	        // r.Duration will be 0 if endless flag has been provided. Otherwise it will have the provided duration time.
   421	        hasDuration := (r.Duration > 0)
   422	        // r.Exactly is > 0 if we use Exactly iterations instead of the duration.
   423	        useExactly := (r.Exactly > 0)
   424	        requestedDuration = "until stop"
   425	        requestedQPS = fmt.Sprintf("%.9g", r.QPS)
   426	        if !hasDuration && !useExactly {
   427	                // Always print that as we need ^C to interrupt, in that case the user need to notice
   428	                _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(r.Out, "Starting at %g qps with %d thread(s) [gomax %d] until interrupted%s\n",
   429	                        r.QPS, r.NumThreads, runtime.GOMAXPROCS(0), extra)
   430	                return //nolint:nakedret // it's fine/cleaner to not repeat all the parameters we just set/we return.
   431	        }
   432	        // else:
   433	        requestedDuration = fmt.Sprint(r.Duration)
   434	        numCalls = int64(r.QPS * r.Duration.Seconds())
   435	        if useExactly {
   436	                numCalls = r.Exactly
   437	                requestedDuration = fmt.Sprintf("exactly %d calls", numCalls)
   438	        }
   439	        if numCalls < 2 {
   440	                log.Warnf("Increasing the number of calls to the minimum of 2 with 1 thread. total duration will increase")
   441	                numCalls = 2
   442	                r.NumThreads = 1
   443	        }
   444	        if int64(2*r.NumThreads) > numCalls {
   445	                newN := int(numCalls / 2)
   446	                log.Warnf("Lowering number of threads - total call %d -> lowering from %d to %d threads", numCalls, r.NumThreads, newN)
   447	                r.NumThreads = newN
   448	        }
   449	        numCalls /= int64(r.NumThreads)
   450	        totalCalls := numCalls * int64(r.NumThreads)
   451	        if useExactly {
   452	                leftOver = r.Exactly - totalCalls
   453	                if log.Log(log.Warning) {

    37	// HTTPRunnerResults is the aggregated result of an HTTPRunner.
    38	// Also is the internal type used per thread/goroutine.
    39	type HTTPRunnerResults struct {
    40	        periodic.RunnerResults
    41	        client     Fetcher
    42	        RetCodes   map[int]int64
    43	        IPCountMap map[string]int // TODO: Move it to a shared results struct where all runner should have this field
    44	        // internal type/data
    45	        sizes       *stats.Histogram
    46	        headerSizes *stats.Histogram
    47	        // exported result
    48	        HTTPOptions
    49	        Sizes       *stats.HistogramData
    50	        HeaderSizes *stats.HistogramData
    51	        Sockets     []int64
    52	        SocketCount int64
    53	        // Connection Time stats
    54	        ConnectionStats *stats.HistogramData
    55	        // HTTP status code to abort the run on (-1 for connection or other socket error)
    56	        AbortOn int
    57	        aborter *periodic.Aborter
    58	}
    59	
    60	// Run tests HTTP request fetching. Main call being run at the target QPS.
    61	// To be set as the Function in RunnerOptions.
    62	func (httpstate *HTTPRunnerResults) Run(ctx context.Context, t periodic.ThreadID) (bool, string) {
    63	        log.Debugf("Calling in %d", t)
    64	        code, size, headerSize := httpstate.client.StreamFetch(ctx)
    65	        log.Debugf("Got in %3d hsz %d sz %d - will abort on %d", code, headerSize, size, httpstate.AbortOn)
    66	        httpstate.RetCodes[code]++
    67	        httpstate.sizes.Record(float64(size))
    68	        httpstate.headerSizes.Record(float64(headerSize))
    69	        if httpstate.AbortOn == code {
    70	                httpstate.aborter.Abort(false)
    71	                log.S(log.Info, "Aborted run because of http code",
    72	                        log.Attr("run", httpstate.RunID), log.Attr("code", code), log.Attr("size", size))
    73	        }
    74	        return codeIsOK(code), strconv.Itoa(code)
    75	}
    76	
    77	// HTTPRunnerOptions includes the base RunnerOptions plus HTTP specific
    78	// options.
    79	type HTTPRunnerOptions struct {
    80	        periodic.RunnerOptions
    81	        HTTPOptions               // Need to call Init() to initialize
    82	        Profiler           string // file to save profiles to. defaults to no profiling
    83	        AllowInitialErrors bool   // whether initial errors don't cause an abort
    84	        // Which status code cause an abort of the run (default 0 = don't abort; reminder -1 is returned for socket errors)
    85	        AbortOn int
    86	}
    87	
    88	func NewErrorResult(o *HTTPRunnerOptions, message string, err error) *HTTPRunnerResults {
    89	        log.LogVf("New error result %s: %v", message, err)
    90	        empty := stats.NewHistogram(0, periodic.DefaultRunnerOptions.Resolution)
    91	        empty.Record(0.)
    92	        empty.Record(0.001) // 2 points to generate a big red block when visualized in browse UI.
    93	        return &HTTPRunnerResults{
    94	                HTTPOptions: o.HTTPOptions,
    95	                RunnerResults: periodic.RunnerResults{
    96	                        StartTime:               time.Now(),
    97	                        RunType:                 o.RunType,
    98	                        RunID:                   o.RunID,
    99	                        ID:                      o.RunnerOptions.ID,
   100	                        ServerReply:             *jrpc.NewErrorReply(message, err),
   101	                        DurationHistogram:       empty.Export(),
   102	                        ErrorsDurationHistogram: empty.Export(),
   103	                },
   104	        }
   105	}

   107	// RunHTTPTest runs an HTTP test and returns the aggregated stats.
   108	//
   109	//nolint:funlen, gocognit, gocyclo, maintidx // yeah it's long and complex, but it does a lot of things.
   110	func RunHTTPTest(o *HTTPRunnerOptions) (*HTTPRunnerResults, error) {
   111	        o.RunType = "HTTP"
   112	        warmupMode := "parallel"
   113	        if o.SequentialWarmup {
   114	                warmupMode = "sequential"
   115	        }
   116	
   117	        connReuseMsg := ""
   118	        if o.ConnReuseRange != [2]int{0, 0} {
   119	                connReuseMsg = fmt.Sprintf("[%d, %d]", o.ConnReuseRange[0], o.ConnReuseRange[1])
   120	        }
   121	        log.S(log.Info, "Starting http test", log.Attr("run", o.RunID), log.Str("url", o.URL),
   122	                log.Attr("threads", o.NumThreads), log.Str("qps", fmt.Sprintf("%.1f", o.QPS)), log.Str("warmup", warmupMode),
   123	                log.Str("conn-reuse", connReuseMsg))
   124	        r := periodic.NewPeriodicRunner(&o.RunnerOptions)
   125	        if o.HTTPOptions.Resolution <= 0 {
   126	                // Set both connect histogram params when Resolution isn't set explicitly on the HTTP options
   127	                // (that way you can set the offset to 0 in connect and to something else for the call)
   128	                o.HTTPOptions.Resolution = r.Options().Resolution
   129	                o.HTTPOptions.Offset = r.Options().Offset
   130	        }
   131	        defer r.Options().Abort()
   132	        numThreads := r.Options().NumThreads // can change during run for c > 2 n
   133	        o.HTTPOptions.UniqueID = o.RunnerOptions.RunID
   134	        o.HTTPOptions.Init(o.URL)
   135	        out := r.Options().Out // Important as the default value is set from nil to stdout inside NewPeriodicRunner
   136	        aborter := r.Options().Stop
   137	        total := HTTPRunnerResults{
   138	                HTTPOptions: o.HTTPOptions,
   139	                RetCodes:    make(map[int]int64),
   140	                IPCountMap:  make(map[string]int),
   141	                sizes:       stats.NewHistogram(0, 100),
   142	                headerSizes: stats.NewHistogram(0, 5),
   143	                AbortOn:     o.AbortOn,
   144	                aborter:     aborter,
   145	        }
   146	        httpstate := make([]HTTPRunnerResults, numThreads)
   147	        // First build all the clients sequentially. This ensures we do not have data races when
   148	        // constructing requests.
   149	        ctx := context.Background()
   150	        for i := range numThreads {
   151	                r.Options().Runners[i] = &httpstate[i]
   152	                // Temp mutate the option so each client gets a logging id
   153	                o.HTTPOptions.ID = i
   154	                // Create a client (and transport) and connect once for each 'thread'
   155	                var err error
   156	                httpstate[i].client, err = NewClient(&o.HTTPOptions)
   157	                // nil check on interface doesn't work
   158	                if err != nil {
   159	                        aborter.RecordStart() // virtual/fake start so when we use the start chan later to wait it doesn't hang
   160	                        return NewErrorResult(o, "init error", err), err
   161	                }
   162	                if o.SequentialWarmup && o.Exactly <= 0 {
   163	                        code, dataLen, headerSize := httpstate[i].client.StreamFetch(ctx)
   164	                        if !o.AllowInitialErrors && !codeIsOK(code) {
   165	                                codeErr := fmt.Errorf("error %d for %s (%d body bytes), thread# %d", code, o.URL, dataLen, i)
   166	                                aborter.RecordStart()
   167	                                return NewErrorResult(o, "initial http error", codeErr), codeErr
   168	                        }
   169	                        if i == 0 && log.LogVerbose() {
   170	                                log.LogVf("first hit of url %s: status %03d, headers %d, total %d", o.URL, code, headerSize, dataLen)
   171	                        }
   172	                }
   173	                // Setup the stats for each 'thread'
   174	                httpstate[i].sizes = total.sizes.Clone()
   175	                httpstate[i].headerSizes = total.headerSizes.Clone()
   176	                httpstate[i].RetCodes = make(map[int]int64)
   177	                httpstate[i].AbortOn = total.AbortOn
   178	                httpstate[i].aborter = total.aborter
   179	        }
   180	        if o.Exactly <= 0 && !o.SequentialWarmup {
   181	                warmup := errgroup{}
   182	                for i := range numThreads {
   183	                        warmup.Go(func() error {
   184	                                code, dataLen, headerSize := httpstate[i].client.StreamFetch(ctx)
   185	                                if !o.AllowInitialErrors && !codeIsOK(code) {
   186	                                        return fmt.Errorf("error %d for %s (%d bytes)", code, o.URL, dataLen)
   187	                                }
   188	                                if i == 0 && log.LogVerbose() {
   189	                                        log.LogVf("first hit of url %s: status %03d, headers %d, total %d", o.URL, code, headerSize, dataLen)
   190	                                }
   191	                                return nil
   192	                        })
   193	                }
   194	                if err := warmup.Wait(); err != nil {
   195	                        return NewErrorResult(o, "warmup error", err), err
   196	                }
   197	        }
   198	        // TODO avoid copy pasta with grpcrunner
   199	        var fc *os.File
   200	        if o.Profiler != "" {
   201	                var err error
   202	                fc, err = os.Create(o.Profiler + ".cpu")
   203	                if err != nil {
   204	                        log.Critf("Unable to create .cpu profile: %v", err)
   205	                        return nil, err
   206	                }
   207	                if err = pprof.StartCPUProfile(fc); err != nil {
   208	                        log.Critf("Unable to start cpu profile: %v", err)
   209	                }
   210	        }
   211	        total.RunnerResults = r.Run()
   212	        if o.Profiler != "" {
   213	                pprof.StopCPUProfile()
   214	                fc.Close()
   215	                fm, err := os.Create(o.Profiler + ".mem")
   216	                if err != nil {
   217	                        log.Critf("Unable to create .mem profile: %v", err)
   218	                        return nil, err
   219	                }
   220	                runtime.GC() // get up-to-date statistics
   221	                if err = pprof.WriteHeapProfile(fm); err != nil {
   222	                        log.Critf("Unable to write heap profile: %v", err)
   223	                }
   224	                fm.Close()
   225	                _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "Wrote profile data to %s.{cpu|mem}\n", o.Profiler)
   226	        }
   227	        // Connection stats, aggregated
   228	        connectionStats := stats.NewHistogram(o.HTTPOptions.Offset.Seconds(), o.HTTPOptions.Resolution)
   229	        // Numthreads may have reduced:
   230	        numThreads = total.RunnerResults.NumThreads
   231	        // But we also must cleanup all the created clients.
   232	        keys := []int{}
   233	        fmt.Fprintf(out, "# Socket and IP used for each connection:\n")
   234	        for i := range numThreads {
   235	                // Get the report on the IP address each thread use to send traffic
   236	                occurrence, connStats := httpstate[i].client.GetIPAddress()
   237	                currentSocketUsed := connStats.Count
   238	                httpstate[i].client.Close()
   239	                // next 2 in 1 (long) line:
   240	                fmt.Fprintf(out, "[%d] %3d socket used, resolved to %s", i, currentSocketUsed, occurrence.AggregateAndToString(total.IPCountMap))
   241	                connStats.Counter.Print(out, ", connection timing")
   242	                total.SocketCount += currentSocketUsed
   243	                total.Sockets = append(total.Sockets, currentSocketUsed)
   244	                // Q: is there some copying each time stats[i] is used?
   245	                for k := range httpstate[i].RetCodes {
   246	                        if _, exists := total.RetCodes[k]; !exists {
   247	                                keys = append(keys, k)
   248	                        }
   249	                        total.RetCodes[k] += httpstate[i].RetCodes[k]
   250	                }
   251	                total.sizes.Transfer(httpstate[i].sizes)
   252	                total.headerSizes.Transfer(httpstate[i].headerSizes)
   253	                connectionStats.Transfer(connStats)
   254	        }
   255	        total.ConnectionStats = connectionStats.Export().CalcPercentiles(o.Percentiles)
   256	        if log.Log(log.Info) {
   257	                total.ConnectionStats.Print(out, "Connection time histogram (s)")
   258	        } else if log.Log(log.Warning) {
   259	                connectionStats.Counter.Print(out, "Connection time (s)")
   260	        }
   261	
   262	        // Sort the ip address form largest to smallest based on its usage count
   263	        ipList := make([]string, 0, len(total.IPCountMap))
   264	        for k := range total.IPCountMap {
   265	                ipList = append(ipList, k)
   266	        }
   267	
   268	        sort.Slice(ipList, func(i, j int) bool {
   269	                return total.IPCountMap[ipList[i]] > total.IPCountMap[ipList[j]]
   270	        })
   271	
   272	        // Cleanup state: (original num thread)
   273	        r.Options().ReleaseRunners()
   274	        sort.Ints(keys)
   275	        totalCount := float64(total.DurationHistogram.Count)
   276	        _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "Sockets used: %d (for perfect keepalive, would be %d)\n", total.SocketCount, r.Options().NumThreads)
   277	        _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "Uniform: %t, Jitter: %t, Catchup allowed: %t\n", total.Uniform, total.Jitter, !total.NoCatchUp)
   278	        _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "IP addresses distribution:\n")
   279	        for _, v := range ipList {
   280	                _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "%s: %d\n", v, total.IPCountMap[v])
   281	        }
   282	        for _, k := range keys {
   283	                _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "Code %3d : %d (%.1f %%)\n", k, total.RetCodes[k], 100.*float64(total.RetCodes[k])/totalCount)
   284	        }
   285	        total.HeaderSizes = total.headerSizes.Export()
   286	        total.Sizes = total.sizes.Export()
   287	        if log.LogVerbose() {
   288	                total.HeaderSizes.Print(out, "Response Header Sizes Histogram")
   289	                total.Sizes.Print(out, "Response Body/Total Sizes Histogram")
   290	        } else if log.Log(log.Warning) {
   291	                total.headerSizes.Counter.Print(out, "Response Header Sizes")
   292	                total.sizes.Counter.Print(out, "Response Body/Total Sizes")
   293	        }
   294	        return &total, nil
   295	}
   296	
   297	// An errgroup is a collection of goroutines working on subtasks that are part of
   298	// the same overall task.
   299	type errgroup struct {
   300	        wg sync.WaitGroup
   301	
   302	        errOnce sync.Once
   303	        err     error
   304	}
   305	
   306	// Wait blocks until all function calls from the Go method have returned, then
   307	// returns the first non-nil error (if any) from them.
   308	func (g *errgroup) Wait() error {
   309	        g.wg.Wait()
   310	        return g.err
   311	}
   312	
   313	// Go calls the given function in a new goroutine.
   314	//
   315	// The first call to return a non-nil error cancels the group; its error will be
   316	// returned by Wait.
   317	func (g *errgroup) Go(f func() error) {
   318	        g.wg.Add(1)
   319	
   320	        go func() {
   321	                defer g.wg.Done()
   322	
   323	                if err := f(); err != nil {
   324	                        g.errOnce.Do(func() {
   325	                                g.err = err
   326	                        })
   327	                }
   328	        }()
   329	}
   330

str_replace_editor create /testbed/reproduce_issue.go --file_text 'package main

import (
	"fmt"
	"math"
	"fortio.org/fortio/stats"
)

func main() {
	// Represents the case with r = 0.000001
	// In the PR description:
	// -r 0.000001
	// The PR description mentions resolution 100ms for p50 when r is 0.000001.
	// Resolution in fortio is typically 0.001 (1ms) by default.
	// If r is used as divider in NewHistogram(offset, r)...
	
	r := 0.000001
	h := stats.NewHistogram(0, r)
	
	// Server waits 500ms and returns.
	// So we record 0.5s multiple times.
	val := 0.5
	for i := 0; i < 100; i++ {
		h.Record(val)
	}
	
	res := h.Export().CalcPercentiles([]float64{50, 75, 90, 99, 99.9})
	
	fmt.Printf("Count: %d\n", res.Count)
	fmt.Printf("Min: %g\n", res.Min)
	fmt.Printf("Max: %g\n", res.Max)
	fmt.Printf("Avg: %g\n", res.Avg)
	
	fmt.Println("Data buckets:")
	for _, b := range res.Data {
		fmt.Printf("  Start: %.17f, End: %.17f, Percent: %g, Count: %d\n", b.Start, b.End, b.Percent, b.Count)
	}
	
	fmt.Println("Percentiles:")
	for _, p := range res.Percentiles {
		fmt.Printf("  Percentile: %g, Value: %g\n", p.Percentile, p.Value)
	}
}
'

package main

import (
'fmt

func main() {
// Represents the case with r = 0.000001
// In the PR description:
// -r 0.000001
// The PR description mentions resolution 100ms for p50 when r is 0.000001.
// Resolution in fortio is typically 0.001 (1ms) by default.
// If r is used as divider in NewHistogram(offset, r)...

r := 0.000001
h := stats.NewHistogram(0, r)

// Server waits 500ms and returns.
// So we record 0.5s multiple times.
val := 0.5
for i := 0; i < 100; i++ {
h.Record(val)
}

res := h.Export().CalcPercentiles([]float64{50, 75, 90, 99, 99.9})

fmt.Printf("Count: %d\n", res.Count)
fmt.Printf("Min: %g\n", res.Min)
fmt.Printf("Max: %g\n", res.Max)
fmt.Printf("Avg: %g\n", res.Avg)

fmt.Println("Data buckets:")
for _, b := range res.Data {
fmt.Printf("  Start: %.17f, End: %.17f, Percent: %g, Count: %d\n", b.Start, b.End, b.Percent, b.Count)
}

fmt.Println("Percentiles:")
for _, p := range res.Percentiles {
fmt.Printf("  Percentile: %g, Value: %g\n", p.Percentile, p.Value)
}
}

import (
	"fmt"

func main() {
	r := 0.000001
	h := stats.NewHistogram(0, r)
	
	val := 0.5
	for i := 0; i < 100; i++ {
		h.Record(val)
	}
	
	res := h.Export().CalcPercentiles([]float64{50, 75, 90, 99, 99.9})

/testbed/reproduce_issue.go
package main

import (
	"fmt"
	"fortio.org/fortio/stats"
)

func main() {
	r := 0.000001
	h := stats.NewHistogram(0, r)
	
	val := 0.5
	for i := 0; i < 100; i++ {
		h.Record(val)
	}
	
	res := h.Export().CalcPercentiles([]float64{50, 75, 90, 99, 99.9})
	
	fmt.Printf("Count: %d\n", res.Count)
	fmt.Printf("Min: %g\n", res.Min)
	fmt.Printf("Max: %g\n", res.Max)
	fmt.Printf("Avg: %g\n", res.Avg)
	
	fmt.Println("Data buckets:")
	for _, b := range res.Data {
		fmt.Printf("  Start: %.17f, End: %.17f, Percent: %g, Count: %d\n", b.Start, b.End, b.Percent, b.Count)
	}
	
	fmt.Println("Percentiles:")
	for _, p := range res.Percentiles {
		fmt.Printf("  Percentile: %g, Value: %g\n", p.Percentile, p.Value)
	}
}
EOF

When a very small resolution is used, the estimated start of a bucket (calculated as `multiplier * boundary + offset`) could end up being smaller than the actual minimum value recorded (`h.Min`). +package main
+
+import (
+"fmt"
+"fortio.org/fortio/stats"
+)
+
+func main() {
+r := 0.000001
+h := stats.NewHistogram(0, r)
+
+val := 0.5
+for i := 0; i < 100; i++ {
+h.Record(val)
+}
+
+res := h.Export().CalcPercentiles([]float64{50, 75, 90, 99, 99.9})
+
+fmt.Printf("Count: %d\n", res.Count)
+fmt.Printf("Min: %g\n", res.Min)
+fmt.Printf("Max: %g\n", res.Max)
+fmt.Printf("Avg: %g\n", res.Avg)
+
+fmt.Println("Data buckets:")
+for _, b := range res.Data {
+fmt.Printf("  Start: %.17f, End: %.17f, Percent: %g, Count: %d\n", b.Start, b.End, b.Percent, b.Count)
+}
+
+fmt.Println("Percentiles:")
+for _, p := range res.Percentiles {
+fmt.Printf("  Percentile: %g, Value: %g\n", p.Percentile, p.Value)
+}
+}
