    29	
    30	// Counter is a type whose instances record values
    31	// and calculate stats (count, average, min, max, and stddev).
    32	type Counter struct {
    33	        Count        int64
    34	        Min          float64
    35	        Max          float64
    36	        Sum          float64
    37	        sumOfSquares float64
    38	}
    39	
    40	// Record records a data point.
    41	func (c *Counter) Record(v float64) {
    42	        c.RecordN(v, 1)
    43	}
    44	
    45	// RecordN efficiently records the same value N times.
    46	func (c *Counter) RecordN(v float64, n int) {
    47	        isFirst := (c.Count == 0)
    48	        c.Count += int64(n)
    49	        switch {
    50	        case isFirst:
    51	                c.Min = v
    52	                c.Max = v
    53	        case v < c.Min:
    54	                c.Min = v
    55	        case v > c.Max:
    56	                c.Max = v
    57	        }
    58	        s := v * float64(n)
    59	        c.Sum += s
    60	        c.sumOfSquares += (s * s)
    61	}
    62	
    63	// Avg returns the average.
    64	func (c *Counter) Avg() float64 {
    65	        if c.Count == 0 {
    66	                return 0.
    67	        }
    68	        return c.Sum / float64(c.Count)
    69	}
    70	
    71	// StdDev returns the standard deviation.
    72	func (c *Counter) StdDev() float64 {
    73	        if c.Count == 0 {
    74	                return 0.
    75	        }
    76	        fC := float64(c.Count)
    77	        sigma := (c.sumOfSquares - c.Sum*c.Sum/fC) / fC
    78	        // should never happen but it does
    79	        if sigma < 0 {
    80	                log.Warnf("Unexpected negative sigma for %+v: %g", c, sigma)
    81	                return 0
    82	        }
    83	        return math.Sqrt(sigma)
    84	}
    85	
    86	// Print prints stats.
    87	func (c *Counter) Print(out io.Writer, msg string) {
    88	        _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "%s : count %d avg %.8g +/- %.4g min %g max %g sum %.9g\n",
    89	                msg, c.Count, c.Avg(), c.StdDev(), c.Min, c.Max, c.Sum)
    90	}
    91	
    92	// Log outputs the stats to the logger.
    93	func (c *Counter) Log(msg string) {
    94	        log.Infof("%s : count %d avg %.8g +/- %.4g min %g max %g sum %.9g",
    95	                msg, c.Count, c.Avg(), c.StdDev(), c.Min, c.Max, c.Sum)
    96	}
    97	
    98	// Reset clears the counter to reset it to original 'no data' state.
    99	func (c *Counter) Reset() {
   100	        var empty Counter
   101	        *c = empty
   102	}
   103	
   104	// Transfer merges the data from src into this Counter and clears src.
   105	func (c *Counter) Transfer(src *Counter) {
   106	        if src.Count == 0 {
   107	                return // nothing to do
   108	        }
   109	        if c.Count == 0 {
   110	                *c = *src // copy everything at once
   111	                src.Reset()
   112	                return
   113	        }
   114	        c.Count += src.Count
   115	        if src.Min < c.Min {
   116	                c.Min = src.Min
   117	        }
   118	        if src.Max > c.Max {
   119	                c.Max = src.Max
   120	        }
   121	        c.Sum += src.Sum
   122	        c.sumOfSquares += src.sumOfSquares
   123	        src.Reset()
   124	}
   125	
   126	// Histogram - written in go with inspiration from https://github.com/facebook/wdt/blob/master/util/Stats.h
   127	
   128	// The intervals are [prev, current] so for "90" (previous is 80) the values in that bucket are >80 and <=90
   129	// that way a cumulative % up to that bucket means X% of the data <= 90 (or 100-X% > 90), works well for max too
   130	// There are 2 special buckets - the first one is from min to and including 0,
   131	// one after the last for value > last and up to max.
   132	var (
   133	        histogramBucketValues = []int32{
   134	                0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6,
   135	                7, 8, 9, 10, 11, // initially increment buckets by 1, my amp goes to 11 !
   136	                12, 14, 16, 18, 20, // then by 2
   137	                25, 30, 35, 40, 45, 50, // then by 5
   138	                60, 70, 80, 90, 100, // then by 10
   139	                120, 140, 160, 180, 200, // line3 *10
   140	                250, 300, 350, 400, 450, 500, // line4 *10
   141	                600, 700, 800, 900, 1000, // line5 *10
   142	                2000, 3000, 4000, 5000, 7500, 10000, // another order of magnitude coarsly covered
   143	                20000, 30000, 40000, 50000, 75000, 100000, // ditto, the end
   144	        }
   145	        numValues  = len(histogramBucketValues)
   146	        numBuckets = numValues + 1 // 1 special first bucket is <= 0; and 1 extra last bucket is > 100000
   147	        firstValue = float64(histogramBucketValues[0])
   148	        lastValue  = float64(histogramBucketValues[numValues-1])
   149	        val2Bucket []int // ends at 1000. Remaining values will not be received in constant time.
   150	
   151	        maxArrayValue      = int32(1000) // Last value looked up as O(1) array, the rest is linear search
   152	        maxArrayValueIndex = -1          // Index of maxArrayValue
   153	)
   154	
   155	// Histogram extends Counter and adds a histogram.
   156	// Must be created using NewHistogram or anotherHistogram.Clone()
   157	// and not directly.
   158	type Histogram struct {
   159	        Counter
   160	        Offset  float64 // offset applied to data before fitting into buckets
   161	        Divider float64 // divider applied to data before fitting into buckets
   162	        // Don't access directly (outside of this package):
   163	        Hdata []int32 // numValues buckets (one more than values, for last one)
   164	}
   165	
   166	// For export of the data:
   167	
   168	// Interval is a range from start to end.
   169	// Interval are left closed, open right expect the last one which includes Max.
   170	// i.e., [Start, End] with the next one being [PrevEnd, NextEnd].
   171	type Interval struct {
   172	        Start float64
   173	        End   float64
   174	}
   175	
   176	// Bucket is the data for 1 bucket: an Interval and the occurrence Count for
   177	// that interval.
   178	type Bucket struct {
   179	        Interval
   180	        Percent float64 // Cumulative percentile
   181	        Count   int64   // How many in this bucket
   182	}
   183	
   184	// Percentile value for the percentile.
   185	type Percentile struct {
   186	        Percentile float64 // For this Percentile
   187	        Value      float64 // value at that Percentile
   188	}
   189	
   190	// HistogramData is the exported Histogram data, a sorted list of intervals
   191	// covering [Min, Max]. Pure data, so Counter for instance is flattened.
   192	type HistogramData struct {
   193	        Count       int64
   194	        Min         float64
   195	        Max         float64
   196	        Sum         float64
   197	        Avg         float64
   198	        StdDev      float64
   199	        Data        []Bucket
   200	        Percentiles []Percentile `json:"Percentiles,omitempty"`
   201	}
   202	
   203	// NewHistogram creates a new histogram (sets up the buckets).
   204	// Divider value can not be zero, otherwise returns zero.
   205	func NewHistogram(offset float64, divider float64) *Histogram {
   206	        if divider == 0 {
   207	                return nil
   208	        }
   209	        h := Histogram{
   210	                Offset:  offset,
   211	                Divider: divider,
   212	                Hdata:   make([]int32, numBuckets),
   213	        }
   214	        return &h
   215	}
   216	
   217	// Val2Bucket values are kept in two different structure
   218	// val2Bucket allows you reach between 0 and 1000 in constant time.
   219	//
   220	//nolint:gochecknoinits // we need to init these.
   221	func init() {
   222	        val2Bucket = make([]int, maxArrayValue)
   223	        maxArrayValueIndex = -1
   224	        for i, value := range histogramBucketValues {
   225	                if value == maxArrayValue {
   226	                        maxArrayValueIndex = i
   227	                        break
   228	                }
   229	        }
   230	        if maxArrayValueIndex == -1 {
   231	                log.Fatalf("Bug boundary maxArrayValue=%d not found in bucket list %v", maxArrayValue, histogramBucketValues)
   232	        }
   233	        idx := 0
   234	        for i := range maxArrayValue {
   235	                if i >= histogramBucketValues[idx] {
   236	                        idx++
   237	                }
   238	                val2Bucket[i] = idx
   239	        }
   240	        // coding bug detection (aka impossible if it works once) until 1000
   241	        if idx != maxArrayValueIndex {
   242	                log.Fatalf("Bug in creating histogram index idx %d vs index %d up to %d", idx, int(maxArrayValue), maxArrayValue)
   243	        }
   244	}
   245	
   246	// lookUpIdx looks for scaledValue's index in histogramBucketValues
   247	// TODO: change linear time to O(log(N)) with binary search.
   248	func lookUpIdx(scaledValue int) int {
   249	        scaledValue32 := int32(scaledValue) //nolint:gosec // we limit ourselves to 32 bits counts.
   250	        if scaledValue32 < maxArrayValue {  // constant
   251	                return val2Bucket[scaledValue]
   252	        }
   253	        for i := maxArrayValueIndex; i < numValues; i++ {
   254	                if histogramBucketValues[i] > scaledValue32 {
   255	                        return i_state_anthropic

   259	        return 0
   260	}
   261	
   262	// Record records a data point.
   263	func (h *Histogram) Record(v float64) {
   264	        h.RecordN(v, 1)
   265	}
   266	
   267	// RecordN efficiently records a data point N times.
   268	func (h *Histogram) RecordN(v float64, n int) {
   269	        h.Counter.RecordN(v, n)
   270	        h.record(v, n)
   271	}
   272	
   273	// Records v value to count times.
   274	func (h *Histogram) record(v float64, count int) {
   275	        // Scaled value to bucketize - we used to subtract epsilon because the interval
   276	        // is open to the left ] start, end ] so when exactly on start it has
   277	        // to fall on the previous bucket: which is more correctly done using
   278	        // math.Ceil()-1 but that doesn't work... so back to epsilon distance.
   279	        scaledVal := (v - h.Offset) / h.Divider
   280	        var idx int
   281	        switch {
   282	        case scaledVal <= firstValue:
   283	                idx = 0
   284	        case scaledVal > lastValue:
   285	                idx = numBuckets - 1 // last bucket is for > last value
   286	        default:
   287	                // else we look it up (with the open interval adjustment)
   288	                svInt := int(scaledVal)
   289	                delta := scaledVal - float64(svInt)
   290	                if delta < 1e-12 {
   291	                        svInt--
   292	                }
   293	                log.Debugf("v %f -> scaledVal %.17f ceil %f delta %g - svInt %d", v, scaledVal, math.Ceil(scaledVal), delta, svInt)
   294	                idx = lookUpIdx(svInt)
   295	        }
   296	        h.Hdata[idx] += int32(count) //nolint:gosec // we limit ourselves to 32 bits counts.
   297	}
   298	
   299	// CalcPercentile returns the value for an input percentile
   300	// e.g., for 90. as input returns an estimate of the original value threshold
   301	// where 90.0% of the data is below said threshold.
   302	// with 3 data points 10, 20, 30; p0-p33.33 == 10, p 66.666 = 20, p100 = 30
   303	// p33.333 - p66.666 = linear between 10 and 20; so p50 = 15
   304	// TODO: consider spreading the count of the bucket evenly from start to end
   305	// so the % grows by at least to 1/N on start of range, and for last range
   306	// when start == end we should get to that % faster.
   307	func (e *HistogramData) CalcPercentile(percentile float64) float64 {
   308	        if len(e.Data) == 0 {
   309	                log.Errf("Unexpected call to CalcPercentile(%g) with no data", percentile)
   310	                return 0
   311	        }
   312	        if percentile >= 100 {
   313	                return e.Max
   314	        }
   315	        // We assume Min is at least a single point so at least covers 1/Count %
   316	        pp := 100. / float64(e.Count) // previous percentile
   317	        if percentile <= pp {
   318	                return e.Min
   319	        }
   320	        for i := range e.Data {
   321	                cur := &e.Data[i]
   322	                if percentile <= cur.Percent {
   323	                        return cur.Start + (percentile-pp)/(cur.Percent-pp)*(cur.End-cur.Start)
   324	                }
   325	                pp = cur.Percent
   326	        }
   327	        return e.Max // not reached
   328	}
   329	
   330	// Export translate the internal representation of the histogram data in
   331	// an externally usable one. Calculates the request Percentiles.
   332	func (h *Histogram) Export() *HistogramData {
   333	        var res HistogramData
   334	        res.Count = h.Counter.Count
   335	        res.Min = h.Counter.Min
   336	        res.Max = h.Counter.Max
   337	        res.Sum = h.Counter.Sum
   338	        res.Avg = h.Counter.Avg()
   339	        res.StdDev = h.Counter.StdDev()
   340	        multiplier := h.Divider
   341	        offset := h.Offset
   342	        // calculate the last bucket index
   343	        lastIdx := -1
   344	        for i := numBuckets - 1; i >= 0; i-- {
   345	                if h.Hdata[i] > 0 {
   346	                        lastIdx = i
   347	                        break
   348	                }
   349	        }
   350	        if lastIdx == -1 {
   351	                return &res
   352	        }
   353	
   354	        // previous bucket value:
   355	        prev := histogramBucketValues[0]
   356	        var total int64
   357	        ctrTotal := float64(h.Count)
   358	        // export the data of each bucket of the histogram
   359	        for i := 0; i <= lastIdx; i++ {
   360	                if h.Hdata[i] == 0 {
   361	                        // empty bucket: skip it, but update prev which is needed for next iteration
   362	                        if i < numValues {
   363	                                prev = histogramBucketValues[i]
   364	                        }
   365	                        continue
   366	                }
   367	                var b Bucket
   368	                total += int64(h.Hdata[i])
   369	                if len(res.Data) == 0 {
   370	                        // First entry, start is min
   371	                        b.Start = h.Min
   372	                } else {
   373	                        b.Start = multiplier*float64(prev) + offset
   374	                }
   375	                b.Percent = 100. * float64(total) / ctrTotal
   376	                if i < numValues {
   377	                        cur := histogramBucketValues[i]
   378	                        b.End = multiplier*float64(cur) + offset
   379	                        prev = cur
   380	                } else {
   381	                        // Last Entry
   382	                        b.Start = multiplier*float64(prev) + offset
   383	                        b.End = h.Max
   384	                }
   385	                b.Count = int64(h.Hdata[i])
   386	                res.Data = append(res.Data, b)
   387	        }
   388	        res.Data[len(res.Data)-1].End = h.Max
   389	        return &res
   390	}
   391	
   392	// CalcPercentiles calculates the requested percentile and adds them to the
   393	// HistogramData. Potential TODO: sort or assume sorting and calculate all
   394	// the percentiles in 1 pass (greater and greater values).
   395	func (e *HistogramData) CalcPercentiles(percentiles []float64) *HistogramData {
   396	        if e.Count == 0 {
   397	                return e
   398	        }
   399	        for _, p := range percentiles {
   400	                e.Percentiles = append(e.Percentiles, Percentile{p, e.CalcPercentile(p)})
   401	        }
   402	        return e
   403	}
   404	
   405	// Print dumps the histogram (and counter) to the provided writer.
   406	// Also calculates the percentile.
   407	func (e *HistogramData) Print(out io.Writer, msg string) {
   408	        if len(e.Data) == 0 {
   409	                _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "%s : no data\n", msg)
   410	                return
   411	        }
   412	        // the base counterpart:
   413	        _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "%s : count %d avg %.8g +/- %.4g min %g max %g sum %.9g\n",
   414	                msg, e.Count, e.Avg, e.StdDev, e.Min, e.Max, e.Sum)
   415	        _, _ = fmt.Fprintln(out, "# range, mid point, percentile, count")
   416	        sep := ">="
   417	        for i := range e.Data {
   418	                b := &e.Data[i]
   419	                if i > 0 {
   420	                        sep = ">" // last interval is inclusive (of max value)
   421	                }
   422	                _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "%s %.6g <= %.6g , %.6g , %.2f, %d\n", sep, b.Start, b.End, (b.Start+b.End)/2., b.Percent, b.Count)
   423	        }
   424	        // print the information of target percentiles
   425	        for _, p := range e.Percentiles {
   426	                _, _ = fmt.Fprintf(out, "# target %g%% %.6g\n", p.Percentile, p.Value)
   427	        }
   428	}
   429	
   430	// Print dumps the histogram (and counter) to the provided writer.
   431	// Also calculates the percentiles. Use Export() once and Print if you
   432	// are going to need the Export results too.
   433	func (h *Histogram) Print(out io.Writer, msg string, percentiles []float64) {
   434	        h.Export().CalcPercentiles(percentiles).Print(out, msg)
   435	}
   436	
   437	// Log Logs the histogram to the counter.
   438	func (h *Histogram) Log(msg string, percentiles []float64) {
   439	        var b bytes.Buffer
   440	        w := bufio.NewWriter(&b)
   441	        h.Print(w, msg, percentiles)
   442	        _ = w.Flush()
   443	        log.Infof("%s", b.Bytes())
   444	}
   445	
   446	// Reset clears the data. Reset it to NewHistogram state.
   447	func (h *Histogram) Reset() {
   448	        h.Counter.Reset()
   449	        // Leave Offset and Divider alone
   450	        for i := 0; i < len(h.Hdata); i++ {
   451	                h.Hdata[i] = 0
   452	        }
   453	}
   454	
   455	// Clone returns a copy of the histogram.
   456	func (h *Histogram) Clone() *Histogram {
   457	        hCopy := NewHistogram(h.Offset, h.Divider)
   458	        hCopy.CopyFrom(h)
   459	        return hCopy
   460	}
   461	
   462	// CopyFrom sets the content of this object to a copy of the src.
   463	func (h *Histogram) CopyFrom(src *Histogram) {
   464	        h.Counter = src.Counter
   465	        h.copyHDataFrom(src)
   466	}
   467	
   468	// copyHDataFrom appends histogram data values to this object from the src.
   469	// Src histogram data values will be appended according to this object's
   470	// offset and divider.
   471	func (h *Histogram) copyHDataFrom(src *Histogram) {
   472	        if h.Divider == src.Divider && h.Offset == src.Offset {
   473	                for i := 0; i < len(h.Hdata); i++ {
   474	                        h.Hdata[i] += src.Hdata[i]
   475	                }
   476	                return
   477	        }
   478	        hData := src.Export()
   479	        for i := range hData.Data {
   480	                data := hData.Data[i]
   481	                h.record((data.Start+data.End)/2, int(data.Count))
   482	        }
   483	}
   484	
   485	// Merge two different histogram with different scale parameters
   486	// Lowest offset and highest divider value will be selected on new Histogram as scale parameters.
   487	func Merge(h1 *Histogram, h2 *Histogram) *Histogram {
   488	        divider := h1.Divider
   489	        offset := h1.Offset
   490	        if h2.Divider > h1.Divider {
   491	                divider = h2.Divider
   492	        }
   493	        if h2.Offset < h1.Offset {
   494	                offset = h2.Offset
   495	        }
   496	        newH := NewHistogram(offset, divider)
   497	        newH.Transfer(h1)
   498	        newH.Transfer(h2)
   499	        return newH
   500	}
   501	
   502	// Transfer merges the data from src into this Histogram and clears src.
   503	func (h *Histogram) Transfer(src *Histogram) {
   504	        if src.Count == 0 {
   505	                return
   506	        }
   507	        if h.Count == 0 {
   508	                h.CopyFrom(src)
   509	                src.Reset()
   510	                return
   511	        }
   512	        h.copyHDataFrom(src)
   513	        h.Counter.Transfer(&src.Counter)
   514	        src.Reset()
   515	}
   516	
   517	// ParsePercentiles extracts the percentiles from string (flag).
   518	func ParsePercentiles(percentiles string) ([]float64, error) {
   519	        percs := strings.Split(percentiles, ",") // will make a size 1 array for empty input!
   520	        res := make([]float64, 0, len(percs))
   521	        for _, pStr := range percs {
   522	                pStr = strings.TrimSpace(pStr)
   523	                if len(pStr) == 0 {
   524	                        continue
   525	                }
   526	                p, err := strconv.ParseFloat(pStr, 64)
   527	                if err != nil {
   528	                        return res, err
   529	                }
   530	                if p <= 0 || p >= 100 {
   531	                        return res, fmt.Errorf("percentile %g must be > 0 and < 100", p)
   532	                }
   533	                res = append(res, p)
   534	        }
   535	        if len(res) == 0 {
   536	                return res, errors.New("list can't be empty")
   537	        }
   538	        log.LogVf("Will use %v for percentiles", res)
   539	        return res, nil
   540	}

+package main
+
+import (
+"fmt"
+"fortio.org/fortio/stats"
+)
+
+func main() {
+r := 0.000001
+h := stats.NewHistogram(0, r)
+
+val := 0.5
+for i := 0; i < 100; i++ {
+h.Record(val)
+}
+
+res := h.Export().CalcPercentiles([]float64{50, 75, 90, 99, 99.9})
+
+fmt.Printf("Count: %d\n", res.Count)
+fmt.Printf("Min: %g\n", res.Min)
+fmt.Printf("Max: %g\n", res.Max)
+fmt.Printf("Avg: %g\n", res.Avg)
+
+fmt.Println("Data buckets:")
+for _, b := range res.Data {
+fmt.Printf("  Start: %.17f, End: %.17f, Percent: %g, Count: %d\n", b.Start, b.End, b.Percent, b.Count)
+}
+
+fmt.Println("Percentiles:")
+for _, p := range res.Percentiles {
+fmt.Printf("  Percentile: %g, Value: %g\n", p.Percentile, p.Value)
+}
+}

+fmt.Printf("Count: %d\n", res.Count)
+fmt.Printf("Min: %g\n", res.Min)
+fmt.Printf("Max: %g\n", res.Max)
+fmt.Printf("Avg: %g\n", res.Avg)
+
+fmt.Println("Data buckets:")
+for _, b := range res.Data {
+fmt.Printf("  Start: %.17f, End: %.17f, Percent: %g, Count: %d\n", b.Start, b.End, b.Percent, b.Count)
+}
+
+fmt.Println("Percentiles:")
+for _, p := range res.Percentiles {
+fmt.Printf("  Percentile: %g, Value: %g\n", p.Percentile, p.Value)
+}
+}
